=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Well well.  Chvátil really sets himself apart once again from pretty much all the other designers in the Industry as far as I can see and IMO. Highly original and innovative once again here with some very nice touches overall and dripping with theme as well. 

Luckily I played this well after the hype machine went out of control so I wasn't so sickened by the hype that it affected my enjoyment, which has happened to me with other titles and I suspect happened to others with this one. You really just have to approach the game with the sole intention of having fun as well although you are also highly challenged to beat the game.  

Like most co-ops group dependancy will dictate how much fun you have, our whole group loved it and we played 6 times in our first night of discovery with this game. That says a lot coming from me anyway and I feel it has a great addictive quality where you want to play again to improve, take on harder challenges or just beat the ones you just lost. The game has a nice tension to it with needing to act "under the gun" and boy can things go to hell in a handbasket in a hurry if your not working together.  

Listening to the instructions I got a little soured when I heard the programmed actions and how you basically plan out all your moves in realtime but dont actually resolve anything until the very end, I figured overall it sounded okay to good but not great. Well it works much better in practice than it seems it would and players really do HAVE to co-operate or you will do very poorly. My brother from the army thinks you could have one guy just be the captain and give out orders all game and things would run smoothly. It might work but it wouldn't be much of a game then and that was NOT the way it was designed to play, doing that would ruin all the fun completely. Also the CD which I thought was largely gimmicky before playing actually works along perfectly in the background keeping you on your toes so not gimmicky since its integral to keep the timing of events during play.   

Where the game shines is players must decide together who is going to go where on the ship and who is going to do what (and due to the cards people have which only they know not everyone can do everything) all as fast as possible since time is always against you and an ever present factor. Being in the right place at the right time and communication are the key key factors and it is not easy to keep it going since you are trying to figure out on your own the best way to contain a threat, play the order of your own cards, refuel a generator etc. Also, it can be hard to coordinate just the conversation since I need something done but then so does player 2, and player 3, help I need help over here, no sorry I'm busy, hey give me that card next turn, alright kill that bastard already! etc - some examples of everyone barking out demands all at the same time in a frenzy.  

There is some chaos effects here that can mess up your plans (and that is largely "exactly" where the fun is during the resolving phase) but here is the thing, the really great part is, they only happen when you or someone screws up! This really had us in stitches when someone was firing lasers into empty space, someone played their card wrong, someone trys to regenerate the shield but has no power, etc. What ends up happening too is some domino effects happen that affect the other players so then you just have to laugh when things get really goofed up. Great laughter came from this actually since everyone knows the moment you realized you goofed how bad the implications might be, then some ridiculing might start, it was just plain silly fun when things got all fubar'ed and made some great gaming moments for us, I was in tears.   

Check out what my buddy Cortexbomb had to say, QUOTE "For some reason I want to liken it to a cocktail party from hell: 4 people are trying to talk to you at once while an out of control DJ is barking out nonsense through his microphone, which is annoying everyone in the room. Meanwhile the exterior of the building is being ravaged by wild animals which the guests are occasionally taking potshots at with their assault rifles." END - LOL nice one! This is mostly a pretty good description and why we all enjoyed the game and why he did not. So looking at that you can hopefully tell whether it is a game for you or not because where some people love it is exactly where lots of others wont.  

Replay was our only slight concern and maybe why I dont have a 9 rating like I think it deserves (though it will get it if I hit 15 plays + and still want to play) as its hard to really knock the game for anything else. I also wonder if it will stay as fun and enjoyable once the freshness wears off(common and this was part of our replay concern). I do think it will benefit from an expansion with maybe some different kind of threats and maybe a new "deck" in the form of another board, just some other new things to do as well as new missions. I think as long as you play it occasionally only, it will have some legs.  

We played with 4 players which I think is probably the minimum and was a great number, 3 won't be as fun since coordinating will be easier but might be passable, 5 should be pretty good. Games only take maybe 20 minutes to play in total. I think this will make a GREAT GATEWAY game and might be my go-to gateway of choice(along with RA), will be tested very soon.

This is my favourite co-op game to date and I think I have played maybe 7 or 8 different ones so far which mostly all were pretty good. Oh and on that note this blows the doors off Pandemic, no contest due to sheer fun level. 

[u]UPDATE[/u] Played with 3 + 2 androids and thought it was fun, also played with 2 players + 3 Androids (not in rules) and its still a fun challenging game. 4 or 5 actual players is better of course but if I knew I was only ever going to have 3 players, I'd probably still buy this. *-).  You are missing the "true" chaos with more real players and the fun of 3 people trying to talk to you all at the same time but the lower numbers are still interesting, at least for now. The time pressure might even make the solo flight worth trying for those interested (I never play solo games but hell I might even try it since its so short)

Ratings would be something like this:

(4:9, 5:9, 3:8, 2:7, 1:6.5)

RATING: 8
Rating after 8 plays.  The always inventive Vlaada Chvatil has produced yet another unique game here.  This time he takes on the cooperative game, and the results aren't really like anything else in my collection.  If you took Robo Rally and combined it with something like Shadows Over Camelot, you're getting close.  It combines the chaos of pre-planning turns with continuous fire fighting, along with the continual ballet of trying to coordinate your actions with the other players (especially power management).  When you add in the chaos of threats coming in at unpredictable times, and the variability of the tracks, it's a fascinating game and one that is fantastically quick.

RATING: 10
Space Alert is hands-down the best game I have ever played. As a co-op game, it effectively solves all of the problems other co-op games have by adding a time limit—no one person runs the show, and you're free to share all of your information.

The game's rules are very solid, unambiguous, and straightforward. You know what you have to do and how to do it, and your group has to figure out how to do it in 10 minutes. With resolution, a game takes 20 minutes, and not a moment of those 20 minutes feels stale.

RATING: 8.5
2011-07-26

Initial Rating: 8.0 (March 2011)

OUTSTANDING game, I can’t believe how many good games Vlaada has designed (Through the Ages, Dungeon Lords, Galaxy Trucker and soon to play Prophecy), he is one of my top 3 favorite designers. I really love Space Alert, the gameplay, the theme, the high interaction between players, the components, everything. It has a huge replayability and it is very simple to learn (after 1 play everything is understood). The play time is short but it packs a lot of fun. I recommend it to everyone. As of today 2011-07-26 I have not played with the highest difficulty due that we always play with new players. 

This game is a keeper; I always want to play it.

Current Rating: 9.0
[hr]
2014-09-29

Space Alert continues to be a top game for me. Perhaps it is my favorite CoOp game EVER. Vlaada is a genius and solved the alpha player issue making sure all the players played at the same time. It is very fun even if the ship got destroyed (by the way, I played Prophecy and it wasn´t the masterwork I was expecting :S).

Space Alert was the first game I ever played with an audio soundtrack, making it very novel for me. The rules are a delight to read, great theme (one of my favorites). Nowadays I feel the game is not so easy to teach. As I wrote years ago, all is understood after one play, but in that play everything will go wrong as there are lots of rules to explain. 

The gameplay is a delight and it is very short (around 12 minutes), there is a lot of chaos and screaming, pure fun. Then you have to see how well you fared (around 10 more minutes).

Best with 5 players. With 4 players it is ok, with less it isn’t fun, although there is another ship designed for three players. I haven’t played with it yet.

I’m kind of sad Space Alert doesn’t hit the table more often. You need a committed group to properly enjoy it, otherwise there will be always new players that need to be taught the game AND you can’t use the higher difficulty enemies for the game.

Next year I will make the commitment to find a game group to play Space Alert. 

Current Rating: 9.0

RATING: 10
This games is a whole new experience in board games. I was really looking forward to trying it since I read about it before being released, and now I can say it doesn't disappoint at all! It is extremely polished and well thought, and the difficulty is incredibly customizable. 

Still I must say in my group we had a lot of initial trouble grasping the general concept of how the game works, and though now I would say it is easy to learn all the rules once you get past the general concept, it can also be very HARD to actually win a game. In any case I feel this is half of its charm, it's a game where you have fun and laughter even if you lose... and sometimes, specially if you loose! Definitely recommended if you like cooperative games, and/or a sci-fi game that creates a very nice atmosphere.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
[b]Update:[/b] I've held off on rating this a 10 for about a year. I've realized that the only thing holding me back was the need to constantly ease in new players with simulations and not full missions. This is one of my favorite games though, and I just love playing full missions with people who know what they're doing. It's so good at what it does, such a humorous, varied, and tight design. 

[b]Tracking My Impressions[/b]: On the second play (first basic game with a grasp of the rules), I had a persistent feeling that I was playing one of the greatest games anyone has ever come up with. Slick, innovative, what's not to like? Still getting a feel for it. Initial rating is a strong "8." 

Update: 3 more plays in one evening. Yep, this is really, really fun. Perhaps more sensitive to group camaraderie than Pandemic, but extremely well done and addictive. 

Update: 3 more plays. Nothing but greatness. A phenomenal game. I think this is just right for four players. It's not quite as much fun when you have to spend some time looking out for the android in a three-player game, and with five the chaos ratchets up perhaps too much. 

[b]Why Space Alert is Awesome[/b]: For 10 minutes, player listen to an audio track that tells them what sorts of threats are endangering the ship (enemy boarding party, malfunctioning equipment, asteroids, space pirates, the occasional intersellar octopus, and more). During that time, everyone tries to coordinate their actions so that when the game is resolved, everyone is in the right place at the right time, adjusting shields, reloading ammunition, firing lasers and rockets, sending out interceptors, activating battlebots, etc. Because of the real-time constraint, you can only discuss the situation so much before your action choices are locked in. When the audio track is over, you go back through each turn (or "minute") of play, and see how well you did based on your programmed actions. The ship might survive, or you may be blown to bits. It all depends on how well you communicated in the heat of the moment. A light-hearted, engaging, fast, well-produced, and extremely well designed game. Highly recommended. 

Update: You really need the right players for this, but if you have them, it's just an incomparable game experience. I'm not sure why I haven't rated this a 10 yet. A few more campaigns are in order. 

Update: I downgraded my rating from a 10 to a 9 only because I never get to play it and even if I did, the play-quality would be greatly lowered by inexperienced crew-mates.

RATING: 7
As a co-op game, SPACE ALERT is one of the best in conceptual execution.  The addition of a CD to simulate a master computer issuing commands & reporting threats is very innovative--way cool!  The CD also doubles as a timing device (instead of a ticking timer/hourglass device) which limits the players to 10 minutes to decide what their actions will be within the scenerio they are playing.  It is like a combo of PANDEMIC & RED NOVEMBER on steroids.  BUT!  The way a player can be lost in the decision of placing action cards during the shuffle of game-play by other players bothers me.  One can easily find themselves becoming a spectator to an interesting board game while watching the scenerio unfold.  Nevertheless, I am impressed by the game's design in so many ways.

RATING: 5.5
Despite the hype, this space co-op game disappointed 2 separate gaming groups of mine. The 10 minute space-romp is quite good, but the resolution phase (which is a step-by-step replay of the frantic 10 minutes but takes another 20 minutes) is boring, fiddly and the anti-climatic way to end the game.

Also, I find the game a tedious exercise in trying to get everyone to time their steps in perfect harmony. And if even 1 person gets it wrong, he has basically ruined the game for everyone. There is no way to recover or change anything, and makes for a terribly boring resolution phase, because all you can do is WATCH but not PLAY. The unforgiving nature of the game means that a simple mistake at the start means that the whole game is lost.

Rules are also quite heavy and because of the tutorial nature of the rules (4 different ways to play the game) made the game extremely hard to learn --- it sounds like an oxymoron, but I prefer to learn the complete game one-shot instead of in separate parts.

RATING: 9
I love this game! The best cooperative game that I have ever played hands down. This game when played correctly solves all of the issues of group think and tasks players with damage control and talking amongst one another. Many times players will band together to form smaller units that will take on looming events or upcoming issues. The other events that take place along the soundtrack add unique features to the game. Also, this game does not suffer from AP as players are tasked with making decisive actions as player's feel the urgency of the real time events taking place. I don't have a bad thing to say about this game at all. I absolutely love it. Non-gamers will think this has a steep learning curve, and will be right. Gamers will understand the basic game mechanics, but may need to play several times to get the feel for the pacing of the game. This is on my short list to purchase.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Won the award for innovative here.

really I don't see anything innovative here. It uses a cd. Squad 7 uses one. I've got an old boardgame that uses a K-7 that keeps running and when the K-7 ends you have to solve the murder or you loose. I can think of several games that use a DVD
It's cooperative. well nothing new. 
Game has different phases... so what.

I have no problem admitting that the game combines the phases well but to call it innovative... 




I like it but resolution face can make or break the game. 
If you start making fun with some moves and add some noises yourselves it is a 9. If everybody remains quiet it is a 7.

comment I made after three plays (Training mission 1,1 and 2)

We played with four ,I was communication officer and Gust who was sitting on my left was captain. So I was playing the fourth cadet as well.Our first mission was terrible. we didn't destroy the first threat. We were doing some uncoordinated stuff ( people didn't consider the effect of the actions of people before them). Pretty funny I have to add. But all in all we came close to making it (7 damage points)

The replay of the first test mission was a piece of cake.
We didn't power the shields anymore at the first time of asking  (they deplete the power needed to fire the lasers too). and had one team (loader and attacker) fighting one threat, while a second team was fighting another threat. the loader could prepare for the third threat.

Hope that all makes sense. Once you've played it it probably does.

We also played the second test mission. No problem at all. With 2 people on the upper decks and two people assisting on the lower deck.

Data exchange was a big laugh the first couple of times.. People wanted to trade cards well after those phases ended. Much too slow :shake:. This was much improved by a simple agreement. We had to agree on exchanges before the actual dataexchange phase. (do you have an Action card you don't need?)

The strange thing is while planning we didn't move our man at all.This is possible because 7 actions aren't to many and you can quickly see where your man is when you look at your planning.

We didn't calculate score. The others wanted to continue playing this one and kept asking what action c was. Because I just had prepared until the first training mission I didn't know the answer and I was a bit worried about the time it would take to figure this out and explaining  it to everyone.

I also read something in calculating the score that possibly meant we played something wrong (players knocked out of the game)I think this comes later into play.

The only slight concern I still have is the resolution phase.
I think this will go away after a couple of more plays. I think it is possible that players don't feel attached anymore because they allready did everything. However this was not the case and the resolution phase with the excellent elevator and shield noises of Tom was great.

What about the "One leader who takes control" problem?
.
Because cards are not shown and the actual playing time is so short I see no real problem with players of the same skill
The captain is not the person who tells everybody what to do. Every player his action has consequences for the next players. Maybe on a higher difficulty the captain will have more options than other players (i don't know), Now the cadets agreed pretty quick on everything.

However the cooperative play with added complexity if you go through the missions is the reason why I can't rate it 8+

People have to be on a same skill level (or understand the options they have available and the consequences for scoring)if you don't want the one leader who takes control problem and to get the most out of the game.

People have to have the same skill in  games to enjoy fully is especially true in cooperative games.  

In the training missions we played everybody was equal. Suppose I knew this game inside out I would start telling people what the optimal actions were instead of suggesting what I feel are the best actions. This I wouldn't do on the easy training missions we played but I probably would do if we raced through the explanation of the game to play one of the more difficult missions.

About the cd.
Much has been talked about the cd and the voice. It does the job. Nothing more nothing less. The cd and sound noises make this pretty stressfull in a good way. Playing with the cd also has the advantage that the time keeper (communications officer) can take the role of one of the cadets. 

All of us want to play this one again.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I hate cooperative games. I HATE THEM. They usually boil down to one outspoken personality dictating to everyone else what they should do. This results in people either grumbling and hating that person or standing up to them and fighting breaks out. Not a fun way to spend an evening. But this takes all my expectations as the latest cooperative craze and disposes of them. My group played 6 games in a row the first time out. That's insane considering we barely play our favorite games more than once a game-night. The difference is the limited time to work out your differences and with the roborally style card play once you make a choice, that's the way it will play out. So people have the freedom to disagree with the dominant player and the dominant player will soon see that working together and letting everyone have their say is the only way to win the game. The other difference is that just because a person has a 'best move to make' doesn't mean their cards will allow them to follow that through. So changes to the best of plans need to be made in order to accomodate the realism of what was dealt. Random factors do abound but it's not about the randomization as much as it's about the puzzle of figuring out how to react to them well. A great theme and a training structure that brings players in gradually leave this as my (begrudgingly) surprise find of the past two years.

RATING: 8.5
The limitations of real-time interaction and special circumstances really help with some of the possible slowdown and group-play of cooperative games; it's too hard to manage everyone else in the time allotted. If I played more often, I might want more threat cards and scenarios for the encounter variety, but the gameplay certainly varies a lot because of other variability (e.g., scenario, threat order, threat vector).  It's too bad to have to teach new people to play with the starter mission simulations, but the games are still pretty fun, even if incomplete.

RATING: 10
Amazing game. For me it wouldn't be fair to say that it lays on the segment of collaborative games: in fact, it redefines this segment. It doesn't have all the typical problems of the collaborative games (the alpha player, despite possible, is often uncounsciously avoided, and if someone assume this role it is only to give general indications, which doesn't kill the fun for the other players). 

In addition, the feeling of "being a team, working all together" is more intense in this game than in any other I have never played. So it is the tension. And the feeling of relieve that invades you after the end of a mission. 

This last statement is specialy true. In fact, I have yet to find a more demanding game than SA: you need to plan your movements taking into account the different threats appearing in real time and forcing you to reconsider your previous actions. And you have to do that in tight coordination with your team mates. Oh! and you have to do that in phases lasting less than 4 minutes. It is not easy, so be prepared: you will lose a lot. And you know what? It will be surprisingly fun.

My favourite game overall. Strongly recommendable.

RATING: 7.5
PROVISIONAL RATING BASED ON PLAYING THE SIMULATIONS WITH 5 PLAYERS

Highly considered design, clear user-friendly layout, great theme (supported by an atmospheric cd . . . which is a fancy sand timer) smooth learning curve and every advancement through training makes me want to play the next stage straight away.

Co-op games sometimes fail because one voice may dominate but the various sections - requiring to break off into smaller teams -  and short decision time mean that it is unlikely. Within the game there is a captain role for one player which would seem to contradict my viewpoint but I (and our group of players) see the role merely as a fancy first player marker.   

Furthermore, in some co-op games a player may be reduced to a minor role but again quick playtime and added complexity (as scenarios evolve demands on each player should increase) suggests that the likelihood is reduced . . . anyway if it does happen you will only be subjected to it for a short time.

Ultimately, Space Alert was the platform for a great night and what more can you ask than that.  It is now my co-op game of choice.

RATING: 8
This game is just plain fun, and I think it's furthered by the fact that there are training missions that baby step you up to the full game; without which it could be a VERY frustrating experience.

Yes it's chaotic; if you're not a fan of programmed movement a-la Robo Rally stay away, or of coop games this is definitely not for you. But we played 4 times in a row and did all of the training and found we wanted to play more and more, regardless of the increasing obstacles.

There's a vast variety of things you can do, and thankfully you can freely converse and plan, and on occasion trade cards.

This one is oozing with theme, magnificent bits, and plenty of fun.

I would certainly say that this one deserves 4-5 players for best effect.

RATING: 8
This game is brilliant in a number of games. It's got  a lot of moving parts, but the "training missions" on the CD make learning the rules about 1,000x times as fun as just reading a rulebook. The "training manual" is a complete hoot. And the business of trying to decide on the correct actions under time constraints is a total blast. 

The CD mission soundtracks themselves are a bit of a missed opportunity - lots more could have been put on them to ad to drama and flavor than just the minimal sound effects and basic 'computer' commands that one actually hears. And success at each mission depends too much on luck of the draw, and can ultimately be a pretty depressing affair, since the only way to win is not to die.

Still, overall this one is a winner and an example of a rare phenomenon indeed - the Euro-style party game.

RATING: N/A
Seems a tad similar to Pandemic in its cooperative play mechanism and collective avoiding damage posed by various threats.

The game is helped by a relatively quick gameplay (10 minutes for each episode). The theme feels very Star Trek like.

It is VERY important to note that although the game says 2-5 players, it should be played with a MINIMUM of 4. Otherwise, gameplay is MUCH less enjoyable (based on the reviews).

Gets plenty of great ratings and lots of love.

Can be a little chaotic.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
8/2011 In the right group it's an excellent cooperative game.  But is it a game?  It's not a game involving planning; it's a planning game, followed by step-by-step sequence-of-events de-breefing wrap-up.  The in-between game element is missing; is's like a one-shot RoboRally of 12 movement+action cards.  Only the planning phase (which really is the entire game) is really tense: time preassure with new information appearing and changing conditions, occuring threats and malfunctions has to be handled.  I like it a lot; re-playability virtually unlimited.  A huge varied treasure cramed into a tiny box and only 30 minutes!

Bought second hand 28/11/2012

RATING: 5
I respect the effort and the originality, but I think the result is way of the mark.
A cooperative roborally is a good idea, but when the designer has one billion ideas, and want them all to be present at the same time in the same game, it becomes almost unplayable.
My group has played lots of heavy (ie. Martin Wallace and the other Vlaada Chvatil) games, but with SA, we hit the roof.

The only way I can see this game being playable (and winable) is if one skilled player takes the lead and basically tells everybody else what to do, and then its not cooperative anymore, but solo-with-assists.

Sorry.

RATING: 8
[Played 56 times]
Original (mixing real time and cooperation), short (about 30 minutes), intense (in the action round), fun (in the resolution round), forcing communication and encouraging coordination.
Well conceived tutorial missions leading to progressive learning of the game.
Lot of variables to enhance replay value: soundtracks, trajectories, enemies, action cards...
Some randomness, but not overwhelming.
Good components.
Limiting factors: you'll need a CD-player and at least one player able to understand the language of the CD. 
It is better with as many players as you may gather.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.9
If you want a cooperative game with a duration of 20 minutes packed with drama and extreme tension, look no furter ! this is it.
Time managment, coordination and prediction are crucial.
VERY original game. We will going down together.. or survive.

+ Great difference with other co-op games is that there is no real dominant player who will dictate what the other players have to do. Much better than 'shadows over Camelot'
There is a constant tension between coordination, fear, doom and chaos. You are always short of time. 
Very good theme. As a child I was a fan of Star Trek. You want to get the role of Kirk or Spock ?
Shooting at aliens and intruders is a blast !
Short playtime is great. You can easily play this game 3 times in one evening.
This game is best with 4 players, but works also very good with 2 or 3 space adventurers. Optimal control of androïd(s) is a real superimposing challenge.
If you want a funny rule book this one would get the n° 1 prize for most hilarious book. The rules  ar full of suprises and funny notes... 
- 
Despite the funny theme, the rules are not easy. Significant learning curve. For me this is not a bad thing because it's a very rewarding game when you just managed to kill the last enemy before you are flying into deep space...

You need always the same core group. 
Not good playable with occasional groups or with players  who take themselves too serious. This is not a eurogame.

update jan 2013. Still remains the best coop game of all time. I consider myself now an old grown up astronaut, ... but still after more than 50 missions, the game doesn't loose its appeal.

======== Approachability Grade: A

Become crew members of a small spaceship scanning dangerous sectors of the galaxy. The missions last just 10 real-time minutes (hyperspace jump, sector scan, hyperspace jump back) and the only task the players have is to protect their ship.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
What amazes me most about the games of Vlaada Chvátil is not just how he comes up with so many wild and unusual ideas for games, but the consistent genius with which he implements them. Getting rid of the achilles heel of co-op games - namely the loudest-guy-in-the-room-syndrome, where one pushy person essentially plays a solitaire game, and you’re just dragged along - by putting your planning on a clock is brilliant enough by itself. But even given that initial insight, I doubt that many people could have come up with a game as good as Space Alert is. Demanding, very replayable and hysterically funny, this game has only a single drawback: unless you continually play with the same group, you’ll probably have to go through the introductory scenarios a bit more often than you’d really like to.

RATING: 7
Space Alert is crazy, tense in a way that's different than any other game I own, fantastically well-produced, and an absolute blast to play. We played the first test run, second test run, and first simulation in one sitting, and I would happily have played more.

That all of the tension and programming and nuttiness is packed into about 20 minutes -- and is easy to teach -- is pretty amazing. It's a unique game with tons of flavor (the rulebook is worth reading for the comedy alone, but it's also an excellent rulebook in its own right), and despite the fact that it doesn't take itself seriously it's an excellent and well thought-out game.

I had expectations based on what I'd read about SA, and based on playing (and loving) Galaxy Trucker, and it lived up to every one of them. What an amazing game!

RATING: 10
My favorite cooperative game.  I've also played Pandemic and Shadows over Camelot (sort of co-op).

What I like:
- It's fast. A game plays in under 20 minutes.
- Time pressure requires every person to think for themselves and you cannot depend on a leader to guide you on everything.
- Difficulty of play can be altered with the basic and advanced threats.
- It's challenging for all player counts.  It definitely gets more challenging the fewer players you have.
- Requires true teamwork to survive.  You need to coordinate actions with others and trust that they will do what you agree on.
- You feel a sense of accomplishment when you survive a mission, and it's fun blaming others when you fail a mission.

What I don't like:
- Lots of pieces to setup/sort.  Playing multiple games in a single session helps reduce setup overhead.
- Sometimes bad card draws can make it impossible to deal with all threats.
- It's hard to have a mix of experienced/beginner players because there's a lot of rules to learn and you may have to go through the tutorial missions for the beginners.
- It takes up a lot of table space.

RATING: 9.5
This used to be one of my top10 favorites, but the difficulty has made it hard to get to table, so I don't know how it has dated.
I love this game. The original realtime co-op hit and still the best one. It's like a very nerdy partygame where you got to do logistic puzzles in middle of chaos. If that sounds boring then let's specify that the logistic puzzles involve blowing up ships. It's pretty much Star Trek: The Boardgame (one of those episodes where their ship is messed up and aliens attack). Sadly it's surprisingly heavy for such a light-hearted and fun game, so teaching it to others or even remembering the rules if you haven't played in a while is a huge pain. I'll give a very small minus for that, but it's still a 10 really. Awesome game.

Expansions:
+Space Alert: The New Frontier 
(Solid expansion if you happen to need more difficulty (and complexity) after beating all the original missions. It has some very good stuff, but definitely for very experienced players only!)

2-Player Comment:
*I must disagree with general BGG opinion - Space Alert is a good 2-player game. There's kind of dummy system, but it's very non-intrusive and also thematic if you imagine the bots as, well, bots (like bit dumber Data that you got to give commands to). It's bit more involved with 2, yes that's a shame as it's quite heavy as is, but it's also slightly easier to co-ordinate with just two "commanders" so it evens out to great, fun experience for all the couples and other 2p gamers out there. Don't skip this because of the player req if you're a co-op fan.

RATING: 8
Kudos for this original game. Finally a co-op that doesn’t suffer from quarterbacking. Well, actually…

Turns out you can play this solo, and once you’ve mastered that, you really would do better to do everything yourself anyway. And as a solo game, it’s fun. But really it’s just ladder logic with increasing challenges/rules. And once you’ve mastered that, there’s no replayability. Still, you get a lot of training missions and real missions and challenges in the box, so it’ll be awhile before you’re bored. 

And since it requires sound (best anyway), it can be hard to play just anywhere. The learning curve is steep, but I love the baby step mission training scenarios they use. Good board, components and rulebook. Theme is great. 

But it only gets a 7 because of no replayability now solo and too hard to introduce to new folks. But for originality and first time experiences, it’s more like a 9. So I split that and put 8.

RATING: 9.5
This was very high on my want list when I first heard about it.
Now that I wrote the German rules and saw the artwork, it is on top position for Essen 2008 (competing with the BSG boardgame).

Basically, Vlaada took a puzzle which has to be solved by all players acting in a coordinated way. The puzzle evolves and changes in play and everything has to happen within a limited time frame.

The game may be prone to all cooperative's games "illness" that a leader will tell all other players what to do. In this case I doubt that it will be much of a problem ...

Of course, "puzzle" does not really nail the excitement of the dangers which threaten your crew and your ship. The game for me is a perfect blend of Galaxy Trucker (mayhem), Pandemic (cooperative play against the game), Squad Seven (stress factor by soundtrack giving orders and limiting the playing time), and Robo Rally (pre-planning of moves)...
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Relatively simple mechanics (move in one of three directions or take one of four actions) hide the ridiculously complex interaction of working with your crew to survive a mission.

You will likely die and die a lot, but each loss gets you a little closer to that first taste of victory.

Space Alert is definitely best with 5 players and the learning curve is steep, but the short time of each mission keeps it from becoming too frustrating or overwhelming.

RATING: 8
This is such a unique game!  As much as I've enjoyed cooperative games in the past, the added time element to this game definitely puts it in a category all by itself and makes it that much more exciting.  Take RoboRally, give it an ever-present time limit, then make it cooperative and the result is this wonderfully fun, challenging, and all-around great game.  The fact that the individual games never seem to last more than 15 or 20 minutes means that we always want to play again and again and again.  Thus far, all of the players were learning it together, so I'm a little worried about what will happen when I add players with different experience levels, but I'm hoping it won't be too much of an issue.  It's a little hard to get this one to the table due to the complexity, but I'm always glad when we do.

RATING: 6
Game in a Nutshell: Plan out actions in real time to attempt to survive 10 minutes of onslaught and malfunction aboard the SS Sitting Duck.

Played as: 4,5 player (First two levels of the training program)

Pros: A uniquely designed game with a fun premise and great sense of humor. It definitely presents a new challenge for a coop and brings a great sense of camaraderie amongst your team of players. The CD is a fun touch and presentation gets an 'A'.

Cons: The challenge of the game is in just trying to understand what's going on. Not tough enough? Try adding more convoluted things to make it more confusing. It's counter intuitive to start into a game and not feel like you grasp what's going on. Yes, I understand that's basically the point, if everyone understood the game perfectly, you could simply get everything laid out logically and you could win virtually everytime. Instead it's a juggling act meant to confuse you... and I don't enjoy that as much as I thought I might. Oh, and it makes for a game that's a complete pain in the ass to teach.

Other: This is not a co-op you can play with anyone. This game is for gamers. I haven't made it all the way to the full game and I don't know if I ever will. It's like the players need to grow together in learning the game which makes it a bit difficult to get a commitment out of people who want to grudge through the growing pains.

Best Use: A gamer's co-op game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I finally played this, after having played Escape the Curse of the Temple. I was surprised that Space Alert feels much calmer and less chaotic in comparison. 

I love that the game offers an experience that is unique, and has a good dose of humour. Communication is key, and everyone is forced to discuss and coordinate. 

I don't like that the rules are a chore to teach and are deliberately convoluted to create chaos. I also found the resolution round a little anti-climatic. Going through the steps and checks felt a little like doing my taxes.

I look forward to playing the game again some day.

RATING: 7
Cool cooperative game where players listen to a CD which alerts them to incoming or on-board threats that they need to handle.  As you're receiving incoming data you need to work as a team: players program their actions: move left, up, down or right, shoot laser, refeul laser or shields, launch robots, etc.  

Once the CD track stops playing you run through everybody's programmed moves one by one.  The planning phase can become chaotic and if one person played a card wrong it could have dire consequences.  Looking forward to playing more scenarios because the first 3 I tried seemed too easy (although good for learning the system).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Live Red November, this is a true co-op game: the players are all playing on one team, and either win or lose the game together.  

Players are the crew of a space ship which is being warped into enemy territory for 10 minutes.  Those 10 minutes are played out in real time, with a CD announcing what threats occur during the 10 minutes, and when they occur.  The players each have 12 turns where they can carry out actions in the ship to defend it (charge shields, fire cannons, generate energy, etc.).  

The cool thing about the gaeme, though, is that during the 10 minute mission players are only creating a plan.  At the end of the 10 minutes the players reset the board, and then carry out all of their actions in turn and player order.  So, if people weren't working in sync, player 1 could try to fire the guns, but if player 2 hadn't already generated some energy, player 1 will just be clicking a dead button.

This game requires a tremendous amount of working together, and the training missions are brilliantly designed to slowly lead people into the full complexity of the game.  

The game is fun; I look forward to playing it more now that I've got the basic mechanics down.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 10
Space Alert is a major favorite of mine. The object is apparently to explore hostile deep space by yelling at everyone enough to forget what it was you were supposed to be doing in the first place. Augment your play with a running playback of the Star Trek: The Next Generation’s ambient engine noise. The first time your group plays, it's wise to have the most experienced player act simply as the instructor. I’m thrilled at how fun this short game is to simply watch, but playing is even more enjoyable. If you’ve ever wanted a realistic game crewing an intergalactic starship- well, you just might be fooled into thinking this game is for you. But if you can occasionally enjoy Galaxy Quest over Star Trek, Starship Troopers over Ender’s Game, or Munchkin over Dungeons & Dragons, then this game is right up your alley. First play a Simulation round, in which you might do reasonably well and not even die. Too bad you’re not supposed to keep score on Simulation Runs. You may even manage to earn a couple extra points for visual confirmation! (Otherwise known as looking out the window. But you do get points for it! Serious!) With your confidence buoyed by the successful Simulation Run, you may attempt a real mission, complete with internal threats, the C button, and robots. Those fickle, fickle robots. Suffice it to say that it will not go as well. For one thing, your ship may be overrun by internal threats alone. For another, trying to keep your security robot teams on task and not end up defending an empty room is... challenging. Stick with what you know, and look out the window again! Then the seeker droid can evade capture, blowing a gaping hole in the side of the ship so big you'll figure the kamikaze fighter will sail on through it. No such luck. 

I hear the expansion is really great, (it scores a 8.75 on BoardGameGeek!) but I really think I need to get better at the game to justify buying it. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9.4
Good old Vlaada Chvátil.  Master of super clever ideas for games and then absolutely ossifying those into an unplayable monolith of rules.  Even doing this game's "short intro" (which was like 8 missions, each adding only a few of the rules of the game) was a serious amount of time and effort to wade through the piles of rules and intricacies.  We had a lot of fun when we eventually got going sort of (Justin and I), but we only got this to table because we set aside a whole afternoon of my vacation time/his visit to get through this game.

So, I will keep this rating of 9.4 because this is an AWESOME idea and a stupidly stressful sort of gameplay... but completely unplayable in the real world with real attention spans and schedules to juggle.

RATING: 6
Designer Vlaada (Vladimír) Chvátil comes up with some very unique games, but somehow they haven't really clicked for me.  Galaxy Trucker and Space Alert are very nicely produced games with lots of bells and whistles but both have left me wanting more. I really thought I would enjoy Space Alert because the idea reminded me of the fun times I had in a simulator at The Christa McAuliffe Space Education Center. A crisis would show up on the main screen and everyone had to do their jobs to prevent the ship from blowing up.

For me, Space Alert failed because the post-mortem to resolve the real-time decisions is boring and methodical contrasted to the mayhem during the real-time events with the CD computer voice.  If the outcome could be worked into the real-time phase that would be cool.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Fantastic sci-fi action game!

Although at first the rules seem intimidating and complex (it comes with two reasonable sized booklets), the game itself is easy to grasp once you understand the basics.

The chaotic planning round is brilliant and with the CD shouting at you and unpredictable enemies popping out on you this game plays fast and hard.

It's so easy for a team of players to make a seemingly good plan that completely falls apart once you play out the events and see what actually happened, as a single card slip or timing error can cost the whole game!

Plays best with all 5 players, but sadly can be quite inaccessible as the steep learning curb means all rookies must be fully "trained" before you can really get to grips with the game (as you won't get time to explain during the missions!).

Best mission score so far: 40 points/5 player mission.

Progressive Rating: 9-10-8-9.

RATING: 7.5
In this co-operative game, players are in a space ship under attack from outside and inside. Player preplan their moves (moving up, down, left, right, or pressing a particular button to fire lasers and so forth), and resolve the actions. A CD is provided for players to follow the instructions. The CD provides a number of variations, and informs you which direction the threats are coming from, and even introduces things like static, which means you cannot talk to your fellow players. 

The rules are funny to read, and the gameplay is very fun. Rating likely to go up after more plays. I definitely want to play this more!

RATING: 9
Ok components, nothing wrong with the theme, on it's face looks like an ALRIGHT GAME but....

Turns out, thanks to revolutionary real-time mechanics, brilliantly balanced gameplay and varied decisions made in a crunch, this is one of the most brilliant, fun, satisfying new games of the last 10 years. There's so much to enjoy with this game that's completely new. It's simultaneously extremely quick to play while still being an absolute brain-burner that's stimulating and engaging without ever be overwhelming or sluggish.

If you like coop games or just really good games, BUY THIS, It's perfect for 4 players but still plays well with 2. I absolutely love this game that is such a mix of good old ideas and amazingly original new ideas!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Space Alert avoids the cooperative genre's one of the biggest problem - one player can play the game for others - by having such a strict time limits that it's practically non-issue. I first thought that CD-soundtrack would be more of a gimmick but because it pushes the game forward in high speed it actually is very essential part of the game. I still dislike the idea that you are more or less forced to have an audio equipment where you play. But as this usually isn't a too big problem it's a very minor minus in otherwise excellent game. (Update: As you can play the soundtrack from a cell phone speaker and thats enough at (otherwise) quiet environment it is really a non-issue).

Playing Space Alert is both very noisy and very fun. Because of time limit and occasional space noise (prevents you from talking) you need to think, coordinate and act fast to pull through the mission. For a good coordination you need someone that is guiding others on the macro level but other players cannot solely rely on the "mastermind" to make all decisions for them and they must act on their own. Because of this, after a successful mission it feels that players really have cooperated. 

An excellent game and definitely one of the best - if not the best - cooperation games.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
I am really starting to dislike Vlaada, the more games I play of his the more headaches I get.  And it comes down to one thing: his rule books.  When the narrative of your rulebooks outweighs the actual outline of the rules, there's an issue.  

This is one of those games that has 2 books, a handbook [for your first few adventures] and the rulebook, which looks amazingly a lot like a properly written rulebook.

The game is simple, like really really simple.  It's relatively intuitive and like most Vlaada games it just plays itself, for better or worst.  So why two books?  It's a pain to get through the book, but at least he highlights the actual rules in the handbook.  If you don't understand what I mean go find a copy of the rulebook online, it's mostly narrative and poorly outlined examples.

So is the game good?  It's like most Vlaada games, very meh worthy.  I have a great board game group and we made the utter most of it, saluting one another by rank, making cliche lines and jokes from sci-fi movies, but those of us who have played Galaxy Trucker, we just felt like merchants.  The game doesn't make you actually feel like you could be on the enterprise or something.

I feel like any license could bogart these mechanics and and concepts and add in some real sci-fi nuances to the game and make a game that everyone will want to play.

So it's a 6.5, the game is good.  Is it worth retail value?  Absolutely not.  
Is it worth the time spent playing?  Yes.  
Does the game have replay value even though it's limited to a set number of tracks?  Surprisingly yes.

So in conclusion, this game feels like you're in space, but you're nothing special, just trying to survive.  The real game is between the players.  The components are Vlaada, you like it or don't.  I don't, it doesn't at all feel like the sort of Sci-Fi I want.  I may even mock up a completely new board for the game based on the Enterprise or something.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Gioco unico nel suo genere: cooperativo che piacerà anche ai non amanti del genere perché in Space Alert ognuno è realmente responsabile delle proprie azioni e della pianificazione da cui ne dipenderanno le sorti dell'intera missione; un lavoro non coordinato porterà ad un'inevitabile sconfitta e distruzione della vostra astronave di classe: bersagio facile. Seguendo delle tracce audio si dovranno contrastare una serie di attacchi nemici che metteranno a dura prova la vostra astronave e l'equipaggio intero. Per un buon lavoro di squadra sarà necessario suddividersi i compiti: capitano, responsabile tattico, addetto alle comunicazioni, ecc. Adrenalina, caos, risate e divertimento sono gli elementi ben miscelati dal grande Vlaada Chvátil che ci presenta un altro originalissimo gioco, anche questa volta il regolamento, che diventa un libricino, è molto divertente. RATING: 8
A very engaging take on the cooperative genre that plays like a mix between RoboRally and Galaxy Trucker.  As usual, the presentation and quality of the game is top-notch, no complaints there.  The Ameritrashers should love this game.

That said, the game isn't a deep-analysis game (which is exactly the sort of game I tend to favor), and it's just ten minutes.  Granted, a *very exciting* ten minutes, but I am still left with a feeling of "that's all?" after a mission.

I'm sure I'll play this game a lot more, and I'll definitely enjoy doing so--keep in mind that it's best with people who can get into their roles--but it will never be a top-ten game.  Nevertheless, thanks to Mr. Chvatil for continuing to bring refreshing ideas to the gaming world.

RATING: 10
Really well-done cooperative game. Players shout at each other for 10 minutes trying to coordinate themselves while a CD tells them the arriving threats. It really gives you the idea to be in danger and presses you. At the same time, it gives you the idea of indecision, while wasting precious minutes deciding whether going left or right, pressing lasers or shields.
Its longevity is guaranteed by mixing randomly drawn action cards (which limit you a little the amount of possible operations), enemies, enemy's speed tracks and CD tracks.
Its only missing thing is competition, being a cooperative game.
IT NEEDS THE RIGHT GROUP.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Non sono obiettivo. Come espresso pubblicamente e in altri commenti, Vlaada Chvatil è uno dei miei autori preferiti: oltre al fatto che si ricordava di me quando l'ho conosciuto ad Essen :), è un autore poliedrico che concepisce bei giochi con ambientazioni e meccaniche molto diverse tra di loro (penso a Galaxy Trucker, Through the Ages, Graenaland, Prophecy).
La sua incursione nel genere cooperativo lascia il segno: uno dei difetti principali di questo genere di giochi è che uno dei giocatori tende a diventare il supervisore del gruppo, trasformando il gioco in un enorme solitario. 
Chvatil risolve questo problema in due modi: istituendo di fatto un capitano, obbligato dal regolamento a fare il supervisore, e mettendo il pepe sulla coda di tutti creando un "gioco lungo 7 minuti che dura mezz'ora".
Space Alert riprende il filone umoristico di Galaxy Trucker già nel manuale, che sembra un estratto della Guida Galattica di Douglas Adams. Il gioco, che ha meccaniche davvero innovative (decisioni in tempo reale, "sbobinatura" della missione, missione fornita da una traccia audio) rendono la partita veloce, snella e tatticamente complessa nel suo svolgimento: nel pochissimo tempo a disposizione, il capitano deve accertarsi che ogni minaccia sia presa in carico, che tutti lavorino in maniera coordinata e che nessuno faccia cavolate. Chi spara cannonate deve contare su quello che al piano di sotto ricarica le batterie, chi alza gli scudi deve sperare che un compagno lanci i droidi di difesa all'attacco degli intrusi. E tutti devono affidarsi al giocatore che, al momento giusto, impedisce al computer di attivare lo screensaver e spegnere la nave!
La combinazione tra minacce, tracciati e tracce audio garantisce elegantemente una longevità adeguata (ho fatto più di 20 partite, una diversa dall'altra). Per i più esperti, che possono regolare la difficoltà del gioco aggiungendo minacce più difficili, è prevista anche una modalità "campagna", che rende il gioco ancora più avvincente.
Credo che il principale difetto del gioco sia l'eterogeneità dei giocatori. Trattandosi di un gioco dove tutti si mettono nella mani degli altri, un inesperto al tavolo di giocatori navigati mette gli altri davanti a un bivio: scegliere missioni più facili o rischiare di non terminarle.
Rimane comunque un piccolo capolavoro, il migliore a mio parere nel genere dei cooperativi.

Some people go gaga for games like this one. I am definitely not one of them!

RATING: 7
Excellent if somewhat chaotic co-op game where you must work together to keep your spacecraft in one piece until your mission is complete. 

The game is played in two parts, the first is in real-time against a soundtrack representing the ships computer which highlights the various threats that you need to deal with by planning out your actions. In second part you work through the actions you and your team selected during the first phase and see if the resulting chaos is sufficient to save your ship from destruction! 

A warning to those who hate to lose, this game is tough! That said, the majority of the fun is in watching your carefully laid plans unravel as your crew blunder about the ship. It should also be mentioned that the rules for the game are reasonably complicated, which may put off some less experienced gamers. However, the game comes with a handbook which walks you through a number of training missions which gradually introduce the various features, so it is pretty easy to pick up if you have time to walk through these scenarios.

Overall Space Alert is superb fun, I would heartily recommend you get a bunch of friends together and give it a try if you can!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Takes awhile to get good at this game. It is very difficult to succeed initially, especially if you don't function well under-pressure. 

You need a light hearted group to play this game, but serious enough to want to succeed. If your group is too serious or competitive, then the frustration level is going to go through the roof. 

It's best to play this game with the mindset that you are going to fail a lot before you succeed. It will take a few games of the same mission with the same play group before you are successful.

Space Alert really boils down to being a dynamic timed group solved puzzle. Yeah that may sound lame to some, but it actually very fun, intense, and crazy. Success and failure is completely up to your team. Nothing random about it (well, except for the mission threats and locations).

It really captures the cooperative team nature while still allowing for individual responsibility and decision making. Other co-ops can at times devolve into one person playing most of the game for everyone else. Not so in Space Alert.

The expansion makes this game rank higher.

solo is ok and good for practice.

edit: after more plays I'm not sure about the staying power of this one. I enjoyed it a lot at first but the shine is wearing off. I suppose the timed puzzle nature of the game isn't appealing to me as it once did. Still a good team work exercise.

RATING: 8.5
I absolutely love a tough nut to crack, and this is a hard game to win.  The preprogrammed moves work really well in this game to add a great deal of tension, hurry and occasional panic.  I love that this is a cooperative game where everyone is scrambling and listening for cues and trying to work together in such a short space of time.  I think the theme is tremendously well matched to the mechanics.

The only reason that I don't want to go out and buy it is because you need a cd player or laptop within arms reach to make it happen.  I wouldn't want the game not to have that, I don't think it would work with out that audio component, and I think the audio cues are some of the funniest and cleverest things about playing the game.  But somehow I find it a little difficult to mentally get over that set-up issue.  

One of the things that attracts me to boardgaming is that I don't need electronics to have a good time.  I find that having so much fun away from gizmos feels very therapeutic since I spend so much time in front of a computer for work.  So the need for electronics is my only disappointment with this game, but it's a significant one.

RATING: 8.5
Another awesome game from the designer of Galaxy Trucker - this time a co-op! Again, the real-time play make this a very tense experience. Probably the most intense game I own, this certainly stands out from most other games.

There are various ways to ramp up the difficulty to maintain interest over time, and it isn't exactly an easy game to begin with. Definitely the sort of game where you need to learn from previous attempts to improve.

The theme & tie-ins with Galaxy Trucker are nicely done. Components are great, and support on the website is good so far (MP3 versions of CDs) with more mission downloads etc. promised for the future.

Plays fine with 2-3 players, though is much harder to learn that way as you also have to manage the androids' moves as well as your own, all in the same limited time! Better experience with 4-5 players.

OWN: Original/1st Czech Games Edition (the one that includes 2xCDs & Scenario Cards). Appears to be compatible enough with the current version of 'The New Frontier' expansion that I own, although cards in expansion are slightly thinner (sleeving solves this!).

RATING: 7
I like it, but teaching the game is like trying to explain quantum physics to gorillas.   Eventually, the people you're trying to teach it to are going to get frustrated and bored, and start wondering why they're trying so hard to get to the fun.  
Games shouldn't be like that if they hope to have a wide audience.  That said, among a group of gamers, it is fairly intuitive after a (losing) play through or two, and the brilliance of the design starts to kind of bleed through.  Slowly.  
I'm not crazy about most games that have a "required soundtrack", but this one implements it well, and joins Escape as one of the few board games that have successfully made this merge without too much pain.  
I like Space Alert.  Don't misunderstand me.  But it is too hard to teach to newish gamers, and therefore, will likely join the pile of games that I'll try to teach in a few years once they've forgotten about their first awful experience with it.  
Hopefully.

RATING: 8
I'll bump the rating up to a solid 8 after getting a few more plays of Space Alert. It's definitely a co-op game and one of the rarer ones where you get those truly celebratory feelings when a friend manages to reload the reactor just in time for you to shoot.

In typical co-op games, everyone is excited by a roll of dice etc, but in this one, someone's actions can have long lasting effects which have ultimately turned the tide of the game.

There's enough hair-raising situations especially with internal threats where you need to briefly metagame the situation to lock down where exactly is the threat going to move at a certain turn and then head there to intercept and destroy it. Read the situation wrong and you're either too late or too early.

It's a fantastic game, but I recommend running through the tutorial and simulated mission (with new players) before embarking on the real one. All of them are still fun to play.

RATING: 9
Space Alert is a blast to play!  I love how frantic and crazy it is when everyone is talking and no one is communicating.  The connection between theme and mechanics is one of the strongest I've noticed in any game that I've played.  The theme and the mechanics need each other and grow organically out of each other.

I love that each player is forced to do his/her own thing and forced to make his/her own decisions.  Space Alert really is a coop that requires the cooperation of every player to win the game.  While it is better to have one decisive person say, "Red player go to the reactor and add some fuel; blue player, make sure you fire the gun," each player must individually decide if that is the right thing to do.  Each player must make choices and if the collective choices of the group are correct, then the ship has a good chance of surviving.  Sometimes the odds are too steep, but that just adds variety and excitement to the most thrilling game that I have ever played.

The only thing stopping me from rating Space Alert a ten is the tendacy for players to get mean and grumpy at each other.  It's only a game!  But the theme can cause players to be so involved that they can get mean and angry at other players more easily than any other game that I have ever played.

RATING: 8
To me there is a fundamental problem with cooperative games; the general syndrome.  In Pandemic, Ghost Stories, even BSG and Shadows it's too easy for one player to end up dictating everyones moves.  All it takes is one comment about a move someone is pondering is not so good, or how there is a great move they didn't see, and suddenly that player becomes the commander, controlling the whole game with the limited feedback of the others players.  I know it doesn't always go this way, but it sometimes does.

Space Alert addresses this beautifully with the time pressure that is introduced from the CD tracks.  Even someone who prefers to control everything isn't going to be able to, and players are just going to have to trust that the other players were competent and did what they needed to do.  This makes the coop experience much more enjoyable as a result. This is easily the best coop experience I've tried.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
Excellent coop game in space from Vlaada Chvatil, who once again manages to perfectly mix a thematic gaming experience with engaging mechanisms.

This game does not suffer alpha gamer problem (because of the real time aspect), but quite high entry hurdle. This game is 50% planning ahead quickly and 50% communication (the key is to tell your team not everything, but only what they need to know). The feeling to barely survive the alien attack is very unique. 

The game has quite a steep learning curve and you need some plays before you can play it well (which is the only complaint I have about Space Alert). However, I have very good experience with introducing one new player in a team of veterans. On the third run (at latest) the newbie is a full team member!

The game is really demanding when planning ahead. It can be very hard to calculate under time pressure, in which round the enemy will do what action and how to react to this. With the different enemy categories, the difficulty level can be very well adjusted. Of course, there may be situations which seem impossible to solve, but it is not so frequent that it is frustrating. In the end this game does certainly not suffer from being too easy.

RATING: N/A
Players are members of space mission, attempting to protect their ship from external threats while it scans a sector of deep space. The game is played in "real-time," as a series of 10-minute missions. An audio CD representing the ship's computer announces incoming threats, causing a chaotic scramble amongst players as they attempt to find a way to maximize the cards each has been dealt to sequentially perform tasks required to counter each threat (move throughout the ship, recharge guns, fire them, etc.). Of course, there is never enough time, and the chaos only makes it more difficult.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
I remember the first time seeing the box for Space Alert. I was killing time in the Ihrysko store in Bratislava and took the game down in their library and had a look through it. After 20 minutes of just looking through the pieces and the rulebook, I still had little idea how to actually "play" the game as I was reading through the "fun parts" where the crew are given their flight orders :)

Fast forward a few months and I picked this up 2nd hand at our local board game meetup in Dublin, when someone arrived in and said he was selling it for €10. Watched a "how to play" video on Youtube and we were ready to go. Myself and my girlfriend played the tutorial missions together and I was hooked. So you can already guess that this will be a positive review!

To start with, the box is sturdy and the artwork is very good. The components are all good quality and there's no colour blind issues to worry about. Once you know what all the pieces do, you'll be able to setup a game very quickly. The instruction manual is very cleverly put together. There are a series of tutorial missions set out. As you pass one, the next mission will introduce a new ability that you can use in the ship. And you need that gentle introduction! There is a lot to understand about how the ship works and it would be very harsh to try and dump it all on the players at once! I feel the teaching level presented is very good to help give players a chance to ease into the game. All in all, great production value.

This game is very much in it's own category. I know of no other games that play like this. After the tutorial missions, there is a lot of hidden information on the board that absolutely requires the players to communicate with each other. And time is of the essence, you're against the clock. It's a very strict clock at that, once he says phase or mission over - that's it. No more playing cards, no going back and changing things. This game can be unforgiving if/when you make a mistake. But that's how it's designed. It's meant to be a struggle and you're meant to lose sometimes. The great bit is that when we've lost, we've sometimes enjoyed the game more than when we won! Seriously, everything will seem to be going to plan and then you'll find something was missed. Someone moved the wrong way, someone didn't charge the reactor, someone miscalculated the health of the enemy. And that's when all you can do is laugh. It's a true co-operative, where everyone wins or everyone loses. 

The timing system is part of the beauty of the game. The non-tutorial missions will last 10 minutes exactly. Once the mp3 says "mission over", it's done. You go back and put your cards faceup and see what you actually did as you play through what actually happened. The playthrough only takes a few minutes and you find out whether you won/lost. And the playtime is a very intense 10 minutes. There's a lot of information coming out and co-ordination to do. You can't have an alpha player, because he has to trust in other people too. In fact, when we play - we always assign the captain role to the newest player in the group. The opposite of having an alpha player at the table! And we've found that works very well. With the optional scoring, the captain is the only person who scores points. At the same time, he's singularly responsible for failure!

In the main game, there's a lot of variability in difficulty and you can tailor it to your own group. There is a free app (android/itunes) available to give random missions beyond the mp3 cd provided, which allows you to tailor the difficulty more exactly. 

The hidden information/chaotic time pressure/requirement for involved co-op play/randomness of enemies/everything really makes this one of my favorite games - possibly the best co-operative game that I know of. I never refuse a game of this and actively suggest this in all my gaming groups - seeking more converts. While some people are intimidated by it, or aren't sure of the look of the game - everyone who's played it has enjoyed it and volunteered for another mission, or two, or three....

Can I highlight any negatives? Sure. Newer players must play the tutorial missions, so the experienced players will end up playing these missions quite a lot. Your group must have the right attitude for this game and be prepared to lose from time to time (as it will happen!). A quiet area is required, so playing in public requires space away from others - or you'll annoy them. But the positives so outweigh these tiny negatives.

Quite simply, an incredible game - and I can't wait to try out the expansion!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
This is one of the best examples of a "group-dependent" game - if you have (1) a dedicated group of 4-5 gamers who meets regularly, (2) who enjoy playing the same game across several meetings, and (3) enjoy puzzly real-time cooperative programming games, then this game is an absolutely fantastic experience!

Unfortunately, if your group doesn't meet all three of these requirements, then it simply won't work.

Why? Well, the game is complex enough (for a real time game) that you need to go through all simulations missions which will slowly add new elements and get the players used to all the mechanics within the game... and only after you played the game [b]eight[/b] times do you finally get a full grasp all the rules and are then ready to play the missions (the standard game) - diving in to the missions would overwhelm and confuse players to points of making the game unplayable.

As such, not having a group of people who meet regularly, want to play the same game several times to learn its nuances, and enjoy its peculiar style of game (which is indeed very peculiar - not many games are real time puzzles where players have to work together to program a complex solution) then the game simply can't take root.

But, my friend, if you are blessed with such a group - and I am fortunate to have one that fits the bill - this is a sublime experience. The synergy you experience as the 4 (or 5) of you try to plan together all our turns, finding the optimal way of dealing with a threat, coordinating threats simultaneously, deciding when to take a loss to stop a larger threat, reacting to unexpected events which cause you to reevaluate your plans, attempting to solve for miscalculations, stressing to verify that you accounted for everything - this is such a truly special experience.

My complaints are mainly conditional - (1) though the gameplay itself is relatively simple, the large number of things you have to consider in a short time span (10 minutes) makes it difficult to learn quickly (it needs to be slowly digested) which make it not a game one can easily introduce, (2) it seems obvious that the game would not be all that interesting with 1-3 players (I would never try it), and (3) some elements are slightly fiddly with its ample bookkeeping.

But if your group meets all 3 of those initial conditions, there there are virtual no complaints (aside from somewhat fiddly bookkeeping) - this is simply the best real time games out there aside from, perhaps, [b]Captain Sonar[/b] - but if I have 4-5 players only, I will be reaching for this one anyway as that serves the 6+ crowd.

Rating is currently at a reserved and cautious 8.5, but I expect it may peak at a 9 eventually.

RATING: 8
Excellent game of dealing with stressful situations in real time with the added bonus that if you loose you don't really die, its just a game.
Threats come in real-time and everyone has to control their characters and coordinate with others to deal with the threats placing what movements and actions they will do at time corresponding to the threats.
After the entire time has elapsed, you go through the entrance of each enemy and each players planned actions to see whether the enemies were correctly dealt with. Usually lots of hilarity ensues after discovering someone went left instead of right or forgot to do 'computer maintenance' etc.

RATING: 10
Battlestations in COOP mode!!

This game is a crazy hoot to play. The setting: a spaceship that is scanning the area that it has warped into. Players listen to a series of prerecorded alert sounds that trigger off events. They then program a hand of cards (ala roborally) in order to deal with the threats. This includes moving around, firing weapons, powering weapons etc.

Once the 10 minute soundtrack finishes, players then resolve all the threats and programmed cards. This is where the fun begins. Erroneous and uncoordinated programming, ship damage etc all add to the tension and agony as players see if they manage to survive the threats.

Great looking components. Fairly easy turn structure. Quickish game. Lots of replaybility. Pity it's so hard to find in English! CZG had a hit with Galaxy Trucker last year and they someone manage to top that this year! Well done.

RATING: 9
Lots of fun, as long as no one takes it too seriously -- it's easy to get blown up because of one mistake.  Time pressure adds a layer of intensity to the game that's quite addictive.  Cooperative, and you must rely on your teammates assurances that they're dealing with something -- you don't have time to double guess them while dealing with your own tasks.
Includes a pleasing solitaire variation where you have all the action cards at your disposal and 4 "androids" to play for in addition to your own activities.  Communication and coordination are no longer a factor, but the decision-making is cranked to 500 percent.

[2012-05-26]
Galaxis roncsderbi és Roborally szerelemgyereke a Space Alert Pandemic kooperációval vegyítve. Egyedi megoldás, hogy az űrjáték CD-vel vezérelt. Egy géphang közli mi történik körülöttünk az űrben, illetve miket csinálhatunk. Némi nyelvtudást igényel, de nem vészes. Űrhajósainkkal a 3x2 részre osztott űrhajónkban tevékenykedünk. Minden teremben több feladatot elvégezhetünk, ezt a Roborally-hoz hasonlóan kártyákkal kell jeleznünk egy idővonalon. A második nehézségen ez 12 lap lerakását jelenti, majd a CD végighallgatása közben. Kb. 5 perc és utána végrehajtjuk a kártyák és ellenséges űrhajók, aszteroidák tevékenységét sorban. Nagy bátran a 3. szinttel próbáltuk kezdeni, de végül a 2-es nehézséget választottuk. Három játékból nem sikerült megmentenünk egyszer sem az űrhajónkat. Nagyon nehéznek tűnik a játék, nagy összeszokottság kell a jó játékhoz, de legalább van bőven kihívás. El sem tudom képzelni az ötödik szint mennyire kilátástalan lehet. A játék rettentő gyors. Fél óra alatt lejátszható egy parti. Egyszerűek a szabályok, logikus a játékmenet. Egyetlen hibának a játékosszámfüggését érzem. Hárman még nem az igazi. Négyen már biztosan jobb és talán öten lehet a legélvezetesebb. Akinek a Galaxis roncsderbi és Roborally tetszett és szereti a kooperációs játékokat az biztosan élvezni fogja a Space Alertet. Egy 7-essel indítok pontban, de még nőhet ha tényleg jobb lesz a játék négyen-öten kipróbálva.

RATING: 6
A unique co-op experience... I much prefer playing against humans rather than a system, so lack of humans to compete against isn't my style... but Space Alert does better for me than most co-ops because the human element is very real. You might not have to crush the other players, but you still must consider them and their psychology to do well on the harder difficulties, and the teamwork element is real (this isn't a solo game)

But still, a co-op. Very clever game, puzzley yet humorous, but not having an opponent makes me quite indifferent about winning/losing, which sucks the tension out for me -- which is also cool cause this game is funny and part of the fun sometimes is to laugh at your defeat (like Galaxy Trucker), but this is one I appreciate more than I enjoy.

(5 Design + 1 Enjoyment)
