RATING: 5
I should first mention that I like Coops, realtime games, and enjoy many preprogrammed games, I also am dying for a great Sci-fi game.  This seemed like a no brainer to me. I won't deny that fans of pre-programming games will probably get a kick out of this.  Lots of logistics to deal with.  This is all about coordination.  But it is this coordination that ultimately makes the game fail for me (though there are other factors as well).  In order to effectively muscle through this it is best to set up a captain that knows the system.  He makes all the decisions, everyone follows orders.  Then what is there for me to do...?

The timing compels the game so that you aren't overly min-maxing, but a good captian will piece together the easy logistics of it all.  Despite the time pressure, I never felt an overwhelming sense of urgency or tension.

It is cool to see the way it plays out in the end, but in some ways it reminds me more of Light Speed where you have the game playing phase and the scoring phase.  Because these elements of play and results are so heavily separated, I ended up feeling a bit bored about halfway through the results phase.  To me this feels like a test where you wait for your paper to come back to find out the results.

There are times in the game where there just isn't much you can do, and you feel like you are waiting around for something to happen.  This tightens up more as you play the more advanced scenarios.  But, when you've made your decisions, it is back to waiting again.

Thematically, it is great.  I love the specific damage.  I love the robots fighting the internal struggle.  Coordinating the power supply is entertaining.  It really works as a fun sim and as a great experience.  It is great to watch it unfold.

It is best to set up a poor communicator as the captain.  A good captain will make it too easy, a bad one will make it more difficult.

Honestly, the most fun thing about this game is pretending that there are interoffice politics.  "Oh, you're gonna get written up for that", "Thanks for the assist, I'll put it in the report", "Do you know how much that's going to cost the company?" 

That said, I just wish it were actually exciting.  It isn't necessary, but I'll occasionally play other people's copies.

I should also should mention that the CD is really annoying.  I find it difficult to understand what is being said sometimes; especially when players are talking to each other, trying to figure out should be done.

RATING: 7
It's like Galaxy Trucker in 3-D.  I think it's an exercise in teamwork, where you must develop a kind of shorthand communication with the other players, while learning to ignore the non-essential sounds of the CD.  Pluses:  it's pretty quick, and presents an interesting real-time puzzle.  Minuses:  the speed aspect and variety of enemies will lead to chaos in most games, which I don't find particularly fun. It seems fun, and I approached it with an open mind, but I didn't fall in love with it.

Update: Starting to grow on me. Raised rating from 6 to 7.

RATING: 7
I should really like this game.  It is well-designed and a very interesting and fun experience with breakneck tension, all things I often love.  This game has some problems though inherent with its design that keep me from being too enthusiastic though.

Mainly, it is hard to get everyone on the same level to play a smooth, complete game.  Introducing all the actions and elements of the game would never work for new players but at the same time, for people like me who have only a weekly game group that not all members show up to all the time, having to play through the training missions over and over again to get everyone to that level isn't the most interesting either.

Also, this game is unforgiving to mistakes, especially early mistakes.  Enter the wrong room or play the wrong action early and everything else can just be a spiral into defeat.  The tripping mechanic is there to alleviate this but delaying all your actions a turn can be just as punishing.  Perhaps my group just hasn't figured out the right strategy, our first games were kind of hectic with everyone running everywhere trying to do everything.  Perhaps we need to stay put and man a station to be more effective.

Losing a game SHOULDN'T be so bad though because the whole game post-setup and teaching should only take 15-20 minutes (10 minutes for the soundtrack and 5-10 to play everything out...even shorter if you lose early).  But I've noticed that after a brutal loss it's hard to get people excited in another go, maybe I need to push for that harder though.  Especially since the game has such a long setup, doing all that for one 15-20 minute play can get irritating.

I'll have to reevaluate this game once everyone is a little more experienced, this is not a forgiving game for beginners but I can see how it could be very rewarding once everyone is a little more experienced and talented at it and all the elements are there to play with.  Especially since you can get several plays in in the time it would take to play most other cooperative games.

RATING: 8.5
Very rarely in the history of board gaming does one come across a game that is truly very unique, and this is one of those rare gems.  Sure, it could be described as a cross between "RoboRally", "Pandemic", and "Galaxy Trucker", yet this game brings something altogether different to the table - a hectic, "real time" game of co-operation and destructive mayhem!  Mind you, at the risk of sounding completely arrogant, I was surprised by how easy this game was.  Playing with 4 experienced and intelligent gamers who communicate very well with each other, it's apparently possible to beat the full missions after only a few training runs.  Okay, it's not "easy", but threads I had read lead me to believe that this game was super-hard.  The production quality of the game is excellent, with my biggest complaint being that nerve gratingly annoying computer voice.  I would have much rather had a soothing female voice, and perhaps some background sound effects of computers beeping, lasers pewing, and footsteps running in between the speaking bits.  Other than that, I have to give big props to the brilliant designer of this truly unique game!  Unfortunately for my wallet, this is one that has some serious expansion potential...  Game design: 4.5/5  Personal enjoyment: 4/5  Total: 8.5/10
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Has to be a 9 because it's so, so good at doing what it does. Space Alert is the dream of RoboRally: tense, pre-programmed movement that's satisfying when it works and perhaps even more satisfying when it doesn't. It is the dream of Pandemic: you are all working together, but you can [i]feel[/i] events spiralling out of control -- and you can't take a breather to think things through or talk it out because the turn has to end in 5, 4, 3, 2, 1...

It's an amazing design and a fantastic, intense experience that must be tried at least once. That said, while losing horribly once is hilarious, I'm not sure that it will be as fun the tenth time. It's just punishing: one mistake can cost you the game, and communication is both critical and very difficult -- we had problems with everyone talking at once.  

The upside is that the time pressure keeps play time short enough that it's quite addictive. It also tends to alleviate Pandemic's "bully problem" because it simply isn't possible for one player to micromanage the whole crew.

Not like any game I own, but a brilliant example of what board games can be.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10

I think the worst part is having to deal with trying to teach new players.  It's really frustrating because they don't know what's happening or how to get involved.  But with a group that knows what's up, this game is AMAZING.  It's like I'm really on a space ship ;)

RATING: 9
One of the most innovative games I've played in a long time.  Making a real-time co-op solves all the complains of "solved" games where an alpha player can control it by themself; there is far too much chaos and uncertainty here for one person to possibly direct all the other crew members exactly.  Everyone needs to be on the ball and engaging; the table is filled with screaming, pointing fingers, and confusion (at least until communications go down :devil: ). The resolution phase is met with groans of dawning comprehension, laughter, and (hopefully) cheers and hi-fives.  A game this exciting and emotionally engaging deserves a 10, particularly when it only takes a half hour.  The only qualm is getting a regular group together to play; otherwise, you'll be running a lot of training missions for the benefit of newbies.

RATING: 4
You're going to make me cooperate *and* put me under timed pressure? One or the other, please. And preferrably, neither.

Really just not a good combination for me, personally. Not something I'm likely to play often. And when I do play it I'll have no better option than just to do whatever I'm told to do by the folks who've played it alot. Otherwise, I'm just being a ninny. 

On the other hand, if you enjoy coops and being under a time limit doesn't set your nerves on edge, this could be the game for you. In many other coops, it's possible that the "deck" can be heavily stacked against you before the game even starts. In Space Alert, there's the feeling that if you can just keep your cool, there's a solution for just about any predicament.

The best part of the game is watching the sequence of events play out after-the-fact.

'5' indicates the level of enjoyment I had with the game. If you enjoy this sort of thing, it could be way up there for you.

RATING: N/A
How to tell CDs apart: The first 2 training missions are 7 minutes long, the rest are around 10 minutes.

Have corrected Stealth Fighter card (correct speed = 3)

Cards appear to be correct length, not the smaller cut ones that don't match the expansion cards.

Amazon review says newer editions have glass pieces that fall over, while old editions had stable wood pieces
http://www.amazon.com/review/RSCOIC4P9PBQP/ref=cm_cr_pr_perm?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B002ALJ9LI

Actually, glass pieces were promo pieces.  New printings actually have PLASTIC pieces (with problematic rounded green cylinders)

http://boardgamegeek.com/thread/971253/newer-printing-having-plastic-cubes

http://boardgamegeekstore.com/products/space-alert-upgrade-set

RATING: 8
A brilliantly original game. The mission CDs, which are very well produced, provide a great deal of frantic decision making. It's actually harder to co-ordinate tactics with the more players that are participating in the game as any strategy you seem to adopt as a team often falls by the wayside as the game progresses. I guess good communication under pressure between players is the key to being successful at this game. The game also provides a large amount of variety due to the combinations provided by the different missions, threats, actions cards etc available. The originality and variety make this one of the best co-operative games available.

RATING: 10
Plays well with three players. I have yet to play with more. Ineptitude has rarely been this much fun. I would not worry if you are unable to consistently find four players. The official three player variant works very well and works for first time players.

The components are excellent, the rulebook is cheesy yet entertaining, and the game plays incredibly quickly once you get the rules down. I did not, however, find it helpful to read the handbook aloud for my play group. The pacing of the rules introductions in the handbook was a bit too slow, and not quite in the right order for my group's sensibilities. However, as I found it very entertaining when I read it the first time, I would still recommend starting with the handbook and going for a straight rules explanation if it feels too slow.

This is certainly a game you want to research and learn ahead of your first play session to make sure things run smoothly and efficiently as the explanation of the rules can be a while and the game plays in a rather unusual manner.

RATING: N/A
‘Space Alert‘, otro juego colaborativo en el que los jugadores deben explorar peligrosos sectores de la galaxia en pequeñas naves. Las misiones duran diez minutos: salto al hiperespacio, escanear el sector, y vuelta al hiperespacio, y lo único que deben lograr es proteger la nave durante el proceso. En un CD se incluyen bandas sonoras de diez minutos que representan los avisos del ordenador central sobre la presencia de amenazas: naves de combate, monstruos interestelares, asteroides, intrusos o averías en la nave… Los jugadores deben decidir quién realizará cada tarea necesaria y coordinarán sus acciones en tiempo real para salir del atolladero. Ofrece varios niveles de dificultad, es muy rejugable, y ofrece una experiencia nunca vista hasta ahora. Cada partida dura unos 30 minutos en total.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Space Alert is another cooperative game that I played three times in November, but contrasts with Ghost Stories because Space Alert is actually a game that I had been eagerly looking forward to trying. It also contrasts with Ghost Stories because it was somewhat disappointing and not a game that I intend to purchase. I think that Vlaada Chvatil is one of the most promising board game designers out there, but didn’t particularly care for his newest offering. My favorite Chvatil game is certainly Galaxy Trucker, including its Rough Road Ahead expansion and The Big Expansion, but I’ve enjoyed the experiences of trying his diverse offerings, from Prophecy to Through the Ages: A Story of Civilization, and now Space Alert. Unlike other promising designers such as Mac Gerdts, Vlaada manages to create an amazingly diverse assortment of games (and while I enjoy Gerdts’ designs, and Imperial was my favorite new game of 2006, I did breathe a sigh of relief when I heard he’d finally abandoned the Rondel in his newest game Princes of Machu Picchu, although there are whisperings that the Rondel is simply hidden in Princes, but I have yet to try it to see for myself). Back to the subject at hand, Space Alert is a fun romp that will inevitably be compared to Space Dealer by many since both games use a CD soundtrack to narrate the game experience. It’s amusing and I’m glad I tried it, but the decision-making just doesn’t measure up to something like Ghost Stories. The actions to choose between are to move left/right/up/down or to push a button A, B, or C. The players certainly have to work together to make sure their actions are timed well together, but you don’t have the same sort of intricate combinations and possibilities that you do in Ghost Stories. You’re forced to spend many of your twelve actions doing nothing if your cards don’t cooperate or to sit in the same room pushing the same button over and over. It’s an experience game and one that’s well worth experiencing, but not one that I want to keep playing, unlike Vlaada’s Galaxy Trucker, which I’ve played 20 times now.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.5
Sure, [thing=38453][/thing] isn't a new game, not even a obscure one that I haven't heard anything about it until now. It so happens that I read a lot regarding [thing=38453][/thing] and the game has been in a on/off relationship with my shopping cart for as long as I can remember.

Why the on?
- Well, I really enjoy [b]cooperative[/b] games. They are my favorite kind of game! O know that I'm a competitive person, and I always play to win when the game requires. But I prefer to beat a game than a person. I like to work together with my friends, and prefer this to burn my brain against them - they are tough to beat! And [thing=38453][/thing] meets this? Yes;
- I also like [b]short games[/b]. I don't mean games with nothing on the bones, but games that give you meaningful choices, that requires smart play, that is [b]fun[/b] to play, all in a tight package. I'm fortune to have found some of these along my gaming quests. And [thing=38453][/thing] meets this? Yes, really well, by the way.

Why not?
- The [b]soundtrack[/b]. I usually play with my gaming group - this means more than one game happening at a time. A loud game, that demands not only a lot of table talk ("Will anyone activates the shields? Do we have enough energy for two shots? An elevator card, do you have one?") but also the need to listen to a soundtrack in English (a minor problem for a lot of you, a great deal of a problem for many of us. I consider myself a good - not great - listener for English words, but with the need to talk with the other players and listen to the soundtrack, I lose a lot of information, specially if the volume isn't high), isn't a great match for multiple gaming tables - anyone playing [thing=38453][/thing] would surely get in the way of the others. I know there is a way to play without the soundtrack, but it feels weird, not within the theme and also requires one player to be the "announcer" - I want everyone involved to play!;
- The [b]frantic play[/b]. I don't mind at all. Many won't also. But there are those that do - players that wants to relax while playing, to take the mind of the everyday rush and have time to ponder about things. In some friday nights, I can even become one of them. I know people that can't handle [thing=16986][/thing]!

These were the considerations I made before I played the game and they all stand now, after I played. [thing=38453][/thing] isn't a game for all, and I guess that even for those that like it, they wouldn't play it everytime they got the chance.

The manual is a blast to read, really fun and useful. The tutorial scenario is a good way to teach players. When we take a step further, we could understand the changes and the added difficulty.

After playing it, would I buy it? Probably not (but, who knows? I did enjoyed it quite a bit), but I'm glad that someone did!

RATING: 9
The way everyone's working together playing an important role, with so much to worry about and the harsh penalties for messing up... it's just fantastic. With a good crew, this makes for a wonderful experience. The best games of this involve an intense countdown, with destroyed plans, hoping that the rockets will hit SOMEthing, seeing the damage token being the one that will ruin everything... and if we somehow make it through alive, it's a miracle to be praised. The adjustable missions make it so you can train a new crew or start hitting stuff head-on. Training and playing in general isn't a very easy feat, but with an experienced crew it's tough to beat.

The expansion makes this all the more addictive, with rewards for victory beyond just winning. As experienced as we are (I've played over 100 times personally) we're still losing far too often, so we've barely touched the red threats yet, but we still love the specializations, the double actions, and of course the badges.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
I've gotten as far as reading the intro instructions and see that it would be a control freak's paradise.  The mechanic is a little odd.  You have an action round where you listen to a recording of incoming threats.  The players use cards similar in theme to Robo Rally that defines a spaceships crews' movement and actions in response to the threats.  Actions include manning shields, laser cannons, and power distribution & generation.  You have 7-10 real-time minutes to plan things during the action round.  After that completes, you move on to the resolution round.  The board is completely reset and you see how well you planned things out.  It's the separation of the action and resolution round that seems a bit wonky.

The control freak part I mentioned is in regards to having an overall plan to handle the events as they come in.  You need a captain that helps direct the actions of other players -- but given resource allocation, current board status and variations of incoming threats, they would need to delegate some of that responsibility or have a really keen mind to keep it all under control.

Looks fun though.

RATING: 5
It's probably a given that a player playing this game for the first time will get lost.  There's a LOT to track in this game, and understanding how it all works together without having played it is a little daunting.  It's not impervious, but any means, but it's a serious challenge.  Once the game gets going, though, it starts to become a little clearer, and you realize that this game is Crisis Management in a Box.  It's another programming game, a la RoboRally, where if you make a mistake at any point, there's a good chance that your whole plan is shot to hell, but if you can get beyond the tragedy of a loss and enjoy the experience of the game, it can be a lot of fun.  I also think that experience will help players better understand how to play their cards based on their information.  At least, I hope so; I'd like to think that it's possible to survive a mission.

2 plays: 4 players

RATING: 10
Co-op games have a tendency to either lend themselves to an alpha running the game for everyone, or needing a traitor to pit players against each other.  Space alert doesn't do those things, instead time pressure means that everyone needs to handle some problems themselves, while communicating only essential information to the other players.  Its a co-op game where the players really have to cooperate with each other, rather than taking orders and playing 'perfectly'.  Combine this with modifiable difficulty and I can never see this game getting old.

RATING: 8
A ton of fun.  Sort of like Robo-Rally, everyone programs all their actions in one phase, then evaluates them in another, watching the chaos unfold.  Unlike Robo-Rally, it's cooperative, so the timed programming phase is frantic coordination mayhem instead of silent concentration.

Shares a lot of thematic elements with Galaxy Trucker, and has a similar out-of-control feel, though with completely different mechanics.  It's the kind of game I would want to always break out with new people to see how they interact and because of the sheer novelty of it, but there's just too much going on to pick up quickly.  So instead it's the sort of game you'll wind up playing with the same group over and over again--while that's sure to still be fun for quite a while, it also limits it a bit in the long run.

Since I don't own the game, I'll always be playing with Heidi and Jason, and I'd love to play with them any time.

RATING: 10
Continues to be excellent - the table talk is great, although you can get so engrossed that you miss computer announcements.  

An expansion for this is a no-brainer - more cards (the decks are thin enough that I tend to see the same threats and trajectories over and over,  although I'm somehow able to shuffle things such that the same cards are always on top!).  Things I'd like to see - more threat cards of all types,  some kind of theming for a particular session (special decks?  special rules? special tracks?)  Alternative systems and ships (maybe a "build your own ship" mode,  with alternative weapon systems).  Have MIRV missiles that hit everything in all zones within range,  or cannons with higher damage but minimum range.  Maybe even cannons that use more power but deal more damage.  Shield Penetration.  Head-to-head team games,  or multi-ship insanity missions?  Or "boss" ships - maybe a threat board with a giant threat to attack or survive.  Maybe a random threat generator - a deck of cards paired with a sandtimer or somesuch.  

Played, and officially awesome. 

Player order cards are smaller than expected (they're the mini-size cards), as are the rest of the bits (pics on BGG are, as usual,  zoomed in and make everything look huge).  Perfectly serviceable though,  played with the glass pieces.  

Seeing things from across the table might be tough,  but seemed okay.  Frantic,  but hilarious.  Already want to play again - rating is tentative,  and it might be a while before I get to play again...

The only con I can see (this is a not insignificant con):  looks like it'll cost about the same as Galaxy Trucker (ie around $70)

On the way (thanks for importing,  FunGamesCafe!)

RATING: 9.7
Hectic and confusing cooperative game played in real-time (10 minute).  Fairly simple in one sense; You use cards to programme your character to do one of a fairly short list of actions: go left, go right, go up/down, press button a, button b, button c, use battlebots.  Behind that is enough complexity that the game comes with six training missions to get you used to everything that you can achieve using those those commands.  This is not a pick-up-and-play game but has potential to be very fun once you half-way know what you're doing.

RATING: 9
Like RoboRally on steroids.  Our group has played through the tutorials and the basic simulation.  Really hard to win.  Not sure if we're ready for the Advanced Simulation or an actual mission yet, based on our results so far.  It's a hoot though!  For the 10 frantic minutes of the Action Round, it's challenging to say the least and requires dedicated cooperation and concentration.  Once the Action Round is completed, everyone breathes a sigh of relief and relaxes to watch the Resolution Round unfold.  You'll laugh and you'll cry, as your best-laid plans often go up in smoke because of a player mistake, or some unanticipated event like damage to a ship component.  The Resolution Round is fun stuff and will generate groans when things don't work out, cheers when they do, and laughs as you find out just how tough it is to save your spaceship.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Space Alert certainly is unique in the inclusion of soundtracks as part of the gameplay.  The frantic and chaotic nature can be attributed to two sources: unfamiliarity with the game itself and with the people you are with.  Once you know how to communicate effectively within the time constraint, as well as what to expect in terms of the different events (the appearance of external threats, data transfer, system malfunction, etc), the occurrences of talking over each other and running out of time become less and less of an issue.  Dominating personalities in co-op games is usually a bad thing to have.  Space Alert legitimizes these players by putting them in the role of "captain" and the "communication officer".  Now it is ok for them to tell people what they should be doing in order to achieve the objective.  Is that a bad thing?  That's for you to decide. 

Ultimately, I feel that Space Alert is more of a gimmick than a revolutionary gaming experience.  It is no different than having another person with a stopwatch dictating a set of instructions to the group.  The replayability is also another matter of concern, especially for those that have become familiar with the game flow.  I know that by our third session we completed our action selections way before the time ran out so we were just sitting around waiting for the audio to finish.  Not a game I feel the need to own.  I may play again with different people but I do think I've already seen all there is to offer here.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
The most wonderful of all co-operative games. You're playing a team of space ship crew members trying to shoot down enemies and fix the problems that occur, all the while a CD spits out new threats coming to destroy the ship.
What makes this game shine is that, unlike other co-ops where it easily happens that the dominating player sort of plays the game for all other players, Space Alert relies on the weakest link in the chain. So much is happening that no single person possibly can steer the details of all: Each player must do his own, and take responsibilty for what may go wrong on his station. The game mechanisms are designed so that what is needed is perfect synchronization of the team mates, and it's very important that certain tasks are performed with a certain timing. Absolutely perfect co-op game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
My group is obsessed with this game. We play 5-8 missions every night we play, which can be up to 2x per week. That's a lot considering how casual we are. Absolutely fantastic. Rulebook includes an amazing set of tutorial missions that walk you through the mechanics at the perfect pace. May seem like there are a lot of rules before you buy, but the game includes just the right amount of information to make it hectic and mess up your plans -- in a fun way, not an overbearing one. Best game I've ever played, even after 70+ missions.

RATING: 8
Very unique game and I’m lucky to have played this with the right group. I can argue that it’s a stressful game that feels more like work and me being more of a lone strategic planner , it not being the kind of game I like.  Despite this feeling the group dynamics and team building it provides is a great merit to the design skills of Vlaada. I could find myself in the role of safety officer and enjoyed seeing how each mission resolved from looking bleak to surprisingly surviving the challenges the game throws at us.

RATING: 8.8
这是本人接触过的最好玩的纯合作类游戏，游戏中玩家需要在短短十分钟时间内处理多起飞船突发事件，参与者在游戏中需要根据自身的特点及位置分工合作，只有优秀的团队才能一步一步化解危机，安全抵达目的。游戏中的最大亮点是自带CD光碟，模拟飞船中央处理器回馈的报警，更是将游戏的拟真紧张气氛推到顶点。。。另外太空警报和银河卡车的美工怎么看怎么像。。。
【关键词】船体设计上/下/左/右，即时时间模拟事件，行动后续结算，能量供应，战斗机器人，内部/外部危机卡，团队工作分配，因果先后关系

【推荐度】极高 【时间团队协作，轻中度美式爱好者
